solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">\n<a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Iranian_history" title="Timeline of Iranian history">Timeline</a><br/><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Iran.svg"><img alt="Flag of Iran.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="630" decoding="async" height="9" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/16px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/24px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flag_of_Iran.svg/32px-Flag_of_Iran.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Iran" title="Portal:Iran">Iran portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Iran" title="Template:History of Iran"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Iran" title="Template talk:History of Iran"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Iran&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Parthian Empire</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;r/: \'ar\' in \'far\'">&#593;&#720;r</span><span title="/&#952;/: \'th\' in \'thigh\'">&#952;</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span><span title="/&#601;n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">&#601;n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; 247&#160;BC &#8211; 224&#160;AD), also known as the <b>Arsacid Empire</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="/&#593;&#720;r/: \'ar\' in \'far\'">&#593;&#720;r</span><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span><span title="/&#618;/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">&#618;</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span></span>/</a></span></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> was a major <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">Iranian</a> political and cultural power in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Iran" title="Ancient Iran">ancient Iran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Its latter name comes from <a href="/wiki/Arsaces_I_of_Parthia" title="Arsaces I of Parthia">Arsaces I of Parthia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> who, as leader of the <a href="/wiki/Parni" title="Parni">Parni</a> tribe, founded it in the mid-3rd century BC when he conquered the region of <a href="/wiki/Parthia" title="Parthia">Parthia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>\'s northeast, then a <a href="/wiki/Satrap" title="Satrap">satrapy</a> (province) under <a href="/wiki/Andragoras_(Seleucid_satrap)" title="Andragoras (Seleucid satrap)">Andragoras</a>, in rebellion against the <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empire</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mithridates_I_of_Parthia" title="Mithridates I of Parthia">Mithridates I of Parthia</a> (r.&#160;c.&#160;171&#8211;138&#160;BC) greatly expanded the empire by seizing <a href="/wiki/Media_(region)" title="Media (region)">Media</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> from the Seleucids. At its height, the Parthian Empire stretched from the northern reaches of the <a href="/wiki/Euphrates" title="Euphrates">Euphrates</a>, in what is now central-eastern <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, to eastern <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>. The empire, located on the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> trade route between the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_Empire" title="Han Empire">Han Empire</a> of <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, became a center of trade and commerce.\n</p><p>The Parthians largely adopted the art, architecture, religious beliefs, and royal insignia of their culturally heterogeneous empire, which encompassed <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Iran" title="Culture of Iran">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic</a>, and regional cultures. For about the first half of its existence, the Arsacid court adopted elements of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Greece" title="Culture of Greece">Greek culture</a>, though it eventually saw a gradual revival of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religion_and_culture_in_ancient_Iran" title="Religion and culture in ancient Iran">Iranian traditions</a>. The Arsacid rulers were titled the "<a href="/wiki/King_of_Kings" title="King of Kings">King of Kings</a>", as a claim to be the heirs to the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>; indeed, they accepted many local kings as <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassals</a> where the Achaemenids would have had centrally appointed, albeit largely autonomous, <a href="/wiki/Satrap" title="Satrap">satraps</a>. The court did appoint a small number of satraps, largely outside Iran, but these satrapies were smaller and less powerful than the Achaemenid potentates. With the expansion of Arsacid power, the seat of central government shifted from <a href="/wiki/Nisa,_Turkmenistan" title="Nisa, Turkmenistan">Nisa</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ctesiphon" title="Ctesiphon">Ctesiphon</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Tigris" title="Tigris">Tigris</a> (south of modern <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>), although several other sites also served as capitals.\n</p><p>The earliest enemies of the Parthians were the <a href="/wiki/Seleucid%E2%80%93Parthian_wars" title="Seleucid&#8211;Parthian wars">Seleucids</a> in the west and the <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> in the east. However, as Parthia expanded westward, they came into conflict with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Armenia_(antiquity)" title="Kingdom of Armenia (antiquity)">Kingdom of Armenia</a>, and eventually the late <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>. Rome and Parthia competed with each other to establish the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Armenian_kings" title="List of Armenian kings">kings of Armenia</a> as their <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">subordinate clients</a>. The Parthians soundly defeated <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Licinius_Crassus" title="Marcus Licinius Crassus">Marcus Licinius Crassus</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carrhae" title="Battle of Carrhae">Battle of Carrhae</a> in 53&#160;BC, and in 40&#8211;39&#160;BC, Parthian forces captured the whole of the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> except <a href="/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon" title="Tyre, Lebanon">Tyre</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">the Romans</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Antony" title="Mark Antony">Mark Antony</a> led a <a href="/wiki/Antony%27s_Parthian_War" title="Antony\'s Parthian War">counterattack</a> against Parthia, although his successes were generally achieved in his absence, under the leadership of his lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Publius_Ventidius_Bassus" title="Publius Ventidius Bassus">Ventidius</a>. Various Roman emperors or their appointed generals invaded Mesopotamia in the course of the ensuing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman-Parthian_Wars" title="Roman-Parthian Wars">Roman-Parthian Wars</a> of the next few centuries. The Romans captured the cities of <a href="/wiki/Seleucia" title="Seleucia">Seleucia</a> and Ctesiphon on multiple occasions during these conflicts, but were never able to hold on to them. Frequent civil wars between Parthian contenders to the throne proved more dangerous to the Empire\'s stability than foreign invasion, and Parthian power evaporated when <a href="/wiki/Ardashir_I" title="Ardashir I">Ardashir I</a>, ruler of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estakhr" title="Estakhr">Istakhr</a> in <a href="/wiki/Persis" title="Persis">Persis</a>, revolted against the Arsacids and killed their last ruler, <a href="/wiki/Artabanus_V_of_Parthia" title="Artabanus V of Parthia">Artabanus V</a>, in 224&#160;AD. Ardashir established the <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sassanid Empire</a>, which ruled Iran and much of the Near East until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_conquests" title="Muslim conquests">Muslim conquests</a> of the 7th century AD, although the Arsacid dynasty lived on through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arsacid_Dynasty_of_Armenia" title="Arsacid Dynasty of Armenia">Arsacid Dynasty of Armenia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arsacid_dynasty_of_Iberia" title="Arsacid dynasty of Iberia">Arsacid dynasty of Iberia</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arsacid_Dynasty_of_Caucasian_Albania" title="Arsacid Dynasty of Caucasian Albania">Arsacid Dynasty of Caucasian Albania</a>; all eponymous branches of the Parthian Arsacids.\n</p><p>Native Parthian sources, written in <a href="/wiki/Parthian_language" title="Parthian language">Parthian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koine_Greek" title="Koine Greek">Greek</a> and other languages, are scarce when compared to Sassanid and even earlier <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid</a> sources. Aside from scattered <a href="/wiki/Cuneiform" title="Cuneiform">cuneiform</a> tablets, fragmentary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ostraca" title="Ostraca">ostraca</a>, rock inscriptions, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drachma" title="Drachma">drachma</a> coins, and the chance survival of some <a href="/wiki/Parchment" title="Parchment">parchment</a> documents, much of Parthian history is only known through external sources. These include mainly <a href="/wiki/Greek_historiography" title="Greek historiography">Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_historiography" title="Roman historiography">Roman histories</a>, but also <a href="/wiki/Chinese_historiography" title="Chinese historiography">Chinese histories</a>, prompted by the Han Chinese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han-Xiongnu_War" title="Han-Xiongnu War">desire to form alliances against the Xiongnu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Parthian_art" title="Parthian art">Parthian artwork</a> is viewed by historians as a valid source for understanding aspects of society and culture that are otherwise absent in textual sources.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" class="toctext">Society and culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Hellenism_and_the_Iranian_revival"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span href="#Writing_and_literature"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">Writing and literature</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Chronological_table_of_Parthian_kings"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Chronological table of Parthian kings</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Parthian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_establishment">Origins and establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Parthian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins and establishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coin_of_Arsaces_I_(1),_Nisa_mint.jpg"><img alt="Two sides of a silver coin. The one on the left bears the imprint of a man\'s head, while the one on the right a sitting individual." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="382" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Coin_of_Arsaces_I_%281%29%2C_Nisa_mint.jpg/220px-Coin_of_Arsaces_I_%281%29%2C_Nisa_mint.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Coin_of_Arsaces_I_%281%29%2C_Nisa_mint.jpg/330px-Coin_of_Arsaces_I_%281%29%2C_Nisa_mint.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Coin_of_Arsaces_I_%281%29%2C_Nisa_mint.jpg/440px-Coin_of_Arsaces_I_%281%29%2C_Nisa_mint.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coin_of_Arsaces_I_(1),_Nisa_mint.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The silver <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drachma" title="Drachma">drachma</a> of <a href="/wiki/Arsaces_I_of_Parthia" title="Arsaces I of Parthia">Arsaces I of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;247&#8211;211&#160;BC) with the Greek language inscription &#913;&#929;&#931;&#913;&#922;&#927;&#933; "of Arsaces"</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Parni_conquest_of_Parthia" title="Parni conquest of Parthia">Parni conquest of Parthia</a></div>\n<p>Before <a href="/wiki/Arsaces_I_of_Parthia" title="Arsaces I of Parthia">Arsaces I of Parthia</a> founded the Arsacid Dynasty, he was chieftain of the <a href="/wiki/Parni" title="Parni">Parni</a>, an ancient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central-Asia" title="Central-Asia">Central-Asian</a> tribe of <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">Iranian peoples</a> and one of several <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> tribes within the confederation of the <a href="/wiki/Dahae" title="Dahae">Dahae</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The Parni most likely spoke an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Iranian_language" title="Eastern Iranian language">eastern Iranian language</a>, in contrast to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Iranian_languages" title="Western Iranian languages">northwestern Iranian language</a> spoken at the time in <a href="/wiki/Parthia" title="Parthia">Parthia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The latter was a northeastern province, first under the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid</a>, and then the <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid</a> empires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> After conquering the region, the Parni adopted <a href="/wiki/Parthian_language" title="Parthian language">Parthian</a> as the official court language, speaking it alongside <a href="/wiki/Middle_Persian" title="Middle Persian">Middle Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aramaic_language" title="Aramaic language">Aramaic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_language" title="Akkadian language">Babylonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sogdian_language" title="Sogdian language">Sogdian</a> and other languages in the multilingual territories they would conquer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Why the Arsacid court retroactively chose 247&#160;BC as the first year of the Arsacid era is uncertain. <a href="/wiki/Adrian_David_Hugh_Bivar" title="Adrian David Hugh Bivar">A.D.H. Bivar</a> concludes that this was the year the Seleucids lost control of Parthia to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andragoras_(3rd_century_BC)" title="Andragoras (3rd century BC)">Andragoras</a>, the appointed <a href="/wiki/Satrap" title="Satrap">satrap</a> who rebelled against them. Hence, Arsaces I "backdated his <a href="/wiki/Regnal_year" title="Regnal year">regnal years</a>" to the moment when Seleucid control over Parthia ceased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_28-29_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_28-29-18">[18]</a></sup> However, Vesta Sarkhosh Curtis asserts that this was simply the year Arsaces was made chief of the Parni tribe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curtis_2007_7_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-curtis_2007_7-19">[19]</a></sup> Homa Katouzian<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katouzian_2009_41_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-katouzian_2009_41-20">[20]</a></sup> and Gene Ralph Garthwaite<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-garthwaite_2005_67_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-garthwaite_2005_67-21">[21]</a></sup> claim it was the year Arsaces conquered Parthia and expelled the Seleucid authorities, yet Curtis<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curtis_2007_7_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-curtis_2007_7-19">[19]</a></sup> and Maria Brosius<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_85_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_85-22">[22]</a></sup> state that Andragoras was not <a href="/wiki/Parni_conquest_of_Parthia" title="Parni conquest of Parthia">overthrown by the Arsacids</a> until 238&#160;BC.\n</p><p>It is unclear who immediately succeeded Arsaces I. Bivar<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and Katouzian<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katouzian_2009_41_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-katouzian_2009_41-20">[20]</a></sup> affirm that it was his brother <a href="/wiki/Tiridates_I_of_Parthia" title="Tiridates I of Parthia">Tiridates I of Parthia</a>, who in turn was succeeded by his son <a href="/wiki/Arsaces_II_of_Parthia" title="Arsaces II of Parthia">Arsaces II of Parthia</a> in 211&#160;BC. Yet Curtis<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curtis_2007_8_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-curtis_2007_8-24">[24]</a></sup> and Brosius<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_86_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_86-25">[25]</a></sup> state that Arsaces II was the immediate successor of Arsaces I, with Curtis claiming the succession took place in 211&#160;BC, and Brosius in 217&#160;BC. Bivar insists that 138&#160;BC, the last regnal year of Mithridates I, is "the first precisely established regnal date of Parthian history."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Due to these and other discrepancies, Bivar outlines <a href="/wiki/List_of_Parthian_kings" title="List of Parthian kings">two distinct royal chronologies</a> accepted by historians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_98-99_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_98-99-27">[27]</a></sup> A fictitious claim was later made from the 2nd-century BC onwards by the Parthians, which represented them as descendants of the Achaemenid king of kings, <a href="/wiki/Artaxerxes_II_of_Persia" title="Artaxerxes II of Persia">Artaxerxes II of Persia</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reign">r</abbr>.&#160;404&#160;&#8211;&#160;358 BC</span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaryaee2012179_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaryaee2012179-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg"><img alt="A map centered on the Mediterranean and Middle East showing the extent of the Roman Republic (Purple), Selucid Empire (Blue), and Parthia (Yellow) around 200&#160;BC." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="1205" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg/300px-Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg/450px-Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg/600px-Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rome-Seleucia-Parthia_200bc.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Parthia" title="Parthia">Parthia</a>, shaded yellow, alongside the <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empire</a> (blue) and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> (purple) around 200&#160;BC</div></div></div>\n<p>For a time, Arsaces consolidated his position in Parthia and <a href="/wiki/Hyrcania" title="Hyrcania">Hyrcania</a> by taking advantage of the invasion of Seleucid territory in the west by <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_III_Euergetes" title="Ptolemy III Euergetes">Ptolemy III Euergetes</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;246&#8211;222&#160;BC) of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Ptolemaic_Egypt" title="History of Ptolemaic Egypt">Egypt</a>. This conflict with Ptolemy, the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Wars#Third_Syrian_War_(246-241_BC)" title="Syrian Wars">Third Syrian War</a> (246&#8211;241&#160;BC), also allowed <a href="/wiki/Diodotus_I" title="Diodotus I">Diodotus I</a> to rebel and form the <a href="/wiki/Greco-Bactrian_Kingdom" title="Greco-Bactrian Kingdom">Greco-Bactrian Kingdom</a> in Central Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_85_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_85-22">[22]</a></sup> The latter\'s successor, <a href="/wiki/Diodotus_II" title="Diodotus II">Diodotus II</a>, formed an alliance with Arsaces against the Seleucids, but Arsaces was temporarily driven from Parthia by the forces of <a href="/wiki/Seleucus_II_Callinicus" title="Seleucus II Callinicus">Seleucus II Callinicus</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;246&#8211;225&#160;BC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_85-86_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_85-86-29">[29]</a></sup> After spending some time in exile among the nomadic <a href="/wiki/Apasiacae" title="Apasiacae">Apasiacae</a> tribe, Arsaces led a counterattack and recaptured Parthia. Seleucus II\'s successor, <a href="/wiki/Antiochus_III_the_Great" title="Antiochus III the Great">Antiochus III the Great</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;222&#8211;187&#160;BC), was unable to immediately retaliate because his troops were engaged in putting down the rebellion of <a href="/wiki/Molon" title="Molon">Molon</a> in <a href="/wiki/Media_(region)" title="Media (region)">Media</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_85-86_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_85-86-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Antiochus III launched a massive campaign to retake Parthia and Bactria in 210 or 209&#160;BC. He was unsuccessful, but did negotiate a peace settlement with Arsaces II. The latter was granted the title of king (<a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Greek</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Basileus" title="Basileus">basileus</a></i>) in return for his submission to Antiochus III as his superior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_29_brosius_2006_86_kennedy_1996_74_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_29_brosius_2006_86_kennedy_1996_74-30">[30]</a></sup> The Seleucids were unable to further intervene in Parthian affairs following increasing encroachment by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> and the Seleucid <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Magnesia" title="Battle of Magnesia">defeat at Magnesia</a> in 190&#160;BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_29_brosius_2006_86_kennedy_1996_74_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_29_brosius_2006_86_kennedy_1996_74-30">[30]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phriapatius_of_Parthia" title="Phriapatius of Parthia">Phriapatius of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;191&#8211;176&#160;BC) succeeded Arsaces II, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phraates_I_of_Parthia" title="Phraates I of Parthia">Phraates I of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;176&#8211;171&#160;BC) eventually ascended the throne. Phraates I ruled Parthia without further Seleucid interference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_and_consolidation">Expansion and consolidation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Parthian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Expansion and consolidation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Seleucid%E2%80%93Parthian_wars" title="Seleucid&#8211;Parthian wars">Seleucid&#8211;Parthian wars</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parthian_Empire.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1035" data-file-width="1359" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Parthian_Empire.gif/300px-Parthian_Empire.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Parthian_Empire.gif/450px-Parthian_Empire.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Parthian_Empire.gif/600px-Parthian_Empire.gif 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parthian_Empire.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parthian Empire timeline including important events and territorial evolution.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xong-e_Ashdar_Parthian_relief.jpg"><img alt="Faded relief carved into the side of a rock. The scene portrays a man on horseback as well as several other characters." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Xong-e_Ashdar_Parthian_relief.jpg/220px-Xong-e_Ashdar_Parthian_relief.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Xong-e_Ashdar_Parthian_relief.jpg/330px-Xong-e_Ashdar_Parthian_relief.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Xong-e_Ashdar_Parthian_relief.jpg/440px-Xong-e_Ashdar_Parthian_relief.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xong-e_Ashdar_Parthian_relief.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A rock-carved <a href="/wiki/Relief" title="Relief">relief</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mithridates_I_of_Parthia" title="Mithridates I of Parthia">Mithridates I of Parthia</a> (r. c.&#160;171&#8211;138&#160;BC), seen riding on horseback, at Kong-e A&#382;dar, city of <a href="/wiki/Izeh" title="Izeh">Izeh</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kh%C5%ABzest%C4%81n_Province" title="Kh&#363;zest&#257;n Province">Kh&#363;zest&#257;n Province</a>, Iran</div></div></div>\n<p>Phraates I is recorded as expanding Parthia\'s control past the <a href="/wiki/Gates_of_Alexander" title="Gates of Alexander">Gates of Alexander</a> and occupied <a href="/wiki/Apamea_Ragiana" title="Apamea Ragiana">Apamea Ragiana</a>. The locations of these are unknown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Yet the greatest expansion of Parthian power and territory took place during the reign of his brother and successor <a href="/wiki/Mithridates_I_of_Parthia" title="Mithridates I of Parthia">Mithridates I of Parthia</a> (r. c.&#160;171&#8211;138 BC),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_86_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_86-25">[25]</a></sup> whom Katouzian compares to <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">Cyrus the Great</a> (d. 530 BC), founder of the Achaemenid Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katouzian_2009_41_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-katouzian_2009_41-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Relations between Parthia and Greco-Bactria deteriorated after the death of Diodotus II, when Mithridates\' forces captured two <a href="/wiki/Eparchy" title="Eparchy">eparchies</a> of the latter kingdom, then under <a href="/wiki/Eucratides_I" title="Eucratides I">Eucratides I</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;170&#8211;145&#160;BC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Turning his sights on the Seleucid realm, Mithridates invaded Media and occupied <a href="/wiki/Ecbatana" title="Ecbatana">Ecbatana</a> in 148 or 147&#160;BC; the region had been destabilized by a recent Seleucid suppression of a rebellion there led by <a href="/wiki/Timarchus" title="Timarchus">Timarchus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> This victory was followed by the Parthian conquest of <a href="/wiki/Babylonia" title="Babylonia">Babylonia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, where Mithridates had coins minted at <a href="/wiki/Seleucia" title="Seleucia">Seleucia</a> in 141&#160;BC and held an official <a href="/wiki/Investiture" title="Investiture">investiture</a> ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curtis_2007_10-11_brosius_2006_86-87_Bivar_1983_34_Garthwaite_2005_76_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-curtis_2007_10-11_brosius_2006_86-87_Bivar_1983_34_Garthwaite_2005_76-35">[35]</a></sup> While Mithridates retired to Hyrcania, his forces subdued the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Elymais" title="Elymais">Elymais</a> and <a href="/wiki/Characene" title="Characene">Characene</a> and occupied <a href="/wiki/Susa" title="Susa">Susa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curtis_2007_10-11_brosius_2006_86-87_Bivar_1983_34_Garthwaite_2005_76_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-curtis_2007_10-11_brosius_2006_86-87_Bivar_1983_34_Garthwaite_2005_76-35">[35]</a></sup> By this time, Parthian authority extended as far east as the <a href="/wiki/Indus_River" title="Indus River">Indus River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Whereas <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hecatompylos" title="Hecatompylos">Hecatompylos</a> had served as the first Parthian capital, Mithridates established royal residences at Seleucia, Ecbatana, <a href="/wiki/Ctesiphon" title="Ctesiphon">Ctesiphon</a> and his newly founded city, Mithradatkert (<a href="/wiki/Nisa,_Turkmenistan" title="Nisa, Turkmenistan">Nisa, Turkmenistan</a>), where the tombs of the Arsacid kings were built and maintained.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Ecbatana became the main summertime residence for the Arsacid royalty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Ctesiphon may not have become the official capital until the reign of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gotarzes_I_of_Parthia" title="Gotarzes I of Parthia">Gotarzes I of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;90&#8211;80&#160;BC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> It became the site of the royal <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">coronation</a> ceremony and the representational city of the Arsacids, according to Brosius.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_103_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_103-40">[40]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Seleucids were unable to retaliate immediately as general <a href="/wiki/Diodotus_Tryphon" title="Diodotus Tryphon">Diodotus Tryphon</a> led a rebellion at the capital <a href="/wiki/Antioch" title="Antioch">Antioch</a> in 142 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> However, by 140&#160;BC <a href="/wiki/Demetrius_II_Nicator" title="Demetrius II Nicator">Demetrius II Nicator</a> was able to launch a counter-invasion against the Parthians in Mesopotamia. Despite early successes, the Seleucids were defeated and Demetrius himself was captured by Parthian forces and taken to Hyrcania. There Mithridates treated his captive with great hospitality; he even married his daughter <a href="/wiki/Rhodogune_of_Parthia" title="Rhodogune of Parthia">Rhodogune of Parthia</a> to Demetrius.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mithradatesi.jpg"><img alt="Two sides of a coin. The side on the left showing the head of a bearded man, while the right a standing individual." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="246" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Mithradatesi.jpg/220px-Mithradatesi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Mithradatesi.jpg/330px-Mithradatesi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Mithradatesi.jpg/440px-Mithradatesi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mithradatesi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drachma" title="Drachma">Drachma</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mithridates_I_of_Parthia" title="Mithridates I of Parthia">Mithridates I of Parthia</a>, showing him wearing a beard and a royal <a href="/wiki/Diadem" title="Diadem">diadem</a> on his head. Reverse side: Greek inscrirption reading &#914;&#913;&#931;&#921;&#923;&#917;&#937;&#931; &#924;&#917;&#915;&#913;&#923;&#927;&#933; &#913;&#929;&#931;&#913;&#922;&#927;&#933; &#934;&#921;&#923;&#917;&#923;&#923;&#919;&#925;&#927;&#931; "of the Great King Arsaces the Philhellene"</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Antiochus_VII_Sidetes" title="Antiochus VII Sidetes">Antiochus VII Sidetes</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;138&#8211;129&#160;BC), a brother of Demetrius, assumed the Seleucid throne and married the latter\'s wife <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra_Thea" title="Cleopatra Thea">Cleopatra Thea</a>. After defeating Diodotus Tryphon, Antiochus initiated a campaign in 130&#160;BC to retake Mesopotamia, now under the rule of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phraates_II_of_Parthia" title="Phraates II of Parthia">Phraates II of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;c.&#160;138&#8211;128&#160;BC). The Parthian general Indates was defeated along the <a href="/wiki/Great_Zab" title="Great Zab">Great Zab</a>, followed by a local uprising where the Parthian governor of Babylonia was killed. Antiochus conquered Babylonia and occupied Susa, where he minted coins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_36-37_curtis_2007_11_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_36-37_curtis_2007_11-43">[43]</a></sup> After advancing his army into Media, the Parthians pushed for peace, which Antiochus refused to accept unless the Arsacids relinquished all lands to him except Parthia proper, paid heavy tribute, and released Demetrius from captivity. Arsaces released Demetrius and sent him to <a href="/wiki/History_of_Syria" title="History of Syria">Syria</a>, but refused the other demands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> By spring 129&#160;BC, the Medes were in open revolt against Antiochus, whose army had exhausted the resources of the countryside during winter. While attempting to put down the revolts, the main Parthian force swept into the region and killed Antiochus in battle. His body was sent back to Syria in a silver coffin; his son Seleucus was made a Parthian hostage<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and a daughter joined Phraates\' <a href="/wiki/Harem" title="Harem">harem</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mithridatesiiyoung.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Mithridatesiiyoung.jpg/220px-Mithridatesiiyoung.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Mithridatesiiyoung.jpg/330px-Mithridatesiiyoung.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Mithridatesiiyoung.jpg/440px-Mithridatesiiyoung.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mithridatesiiyoung.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Drachma of <a href="/wiki/Mithridates_II_of_Parthia" title="Mithridates II of Parthia">Mithridates II of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;c.&#160;124&#8211;90&#160;BC). Reverse side: goddess <a href="/wiki/Tyche" title="Tyche">Tyche</a>/<a href="/wiki/Khvarenah" title="Khvarenah">Khvarenah</a> holding a small <a href="/wiki/Nike_(mythology)" title="Nike (mythology)">Nike</a> offering a wreath; inscription reading [&#914;&#913;&#931;&#921;&#923;&#917;&#937;&#931;] &#913;&#929;&#931;&#913;&#922;&#927;&#933; &#917;&#928;&#921;&#934;&#913;&#925;&#927;&#933;&#931; &#934;&#921;&#923;&#917;&#923;&#923;&#919;&#925;&#927;&#931; "of Renowned/Manifest [King] Arsaces the Philhellene.</div></div></div>\n<p>While the Parthians regained the territories lost in the west, another threat arose in the east. In 177&#8211;176&#160;BC the nomadic confederation of the <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a> dislodged the nomadic <a href="/wiki/Yuezhi" title="Yuezhi">Yuezhi</a> from their homelands in what is now <a href="/wiki/Gansu" title="Gansu">Gansu</a> province in <a href="/wiki/Northwest_China" title="Northwest China">Northwest China</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> the Yuezhi then migrated west into Bactria and displaced the <a href="/wiki/Saka" title="Saka">Saka</a> (Scythian) tribes. The Saka were forced to move further west, where they invaded the Parthian Empire\'s northeastern borders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Mithridates was thus forced to retire to Hyrcania after his conquest of Mesopotamia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_89_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_89-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some of the Saka were enlisted in Phraates\' forces against Antiochus. However, they arrived too late to engage in the conflict. When Phraates refused to pay their wages, the Saka revolted, which he tried to put down with the aid of former Seleucid soldiers, yet they too abandoned Phraates and joined sides with the Saka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Phraates II marched against this combined force, but he was killed in battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The Roman historian <a href="/wiki/Justin_(historian)" title="Justin (historian)">Justin</a> reports that his successor <a href="/wiki/Artabanus_I_of_Parthia" title="Artabanus I of Parthia">Artabanus I of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;128&#8211;124&#160;BC) shared a similar fate fighting nomads in the east. He claims Artabanus was killed by the Tokhari (identified as the Yuezhi), although Bivar believes Justin conflated them with the Saka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mithridates_II_of_Parthia" title="Mithridates II of Parthia">Mithridates II of Parthia</a> (r. c.&#160;124&#8211;90&#160;BC) later recovered the lands lost to the Saka in <a href="/wiki/Sistan" title="Sistan">Sistan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Silk_from_Mawangdui_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Silk_from_Mawangdui_2.jpg/220px-Silk_from_Mawangdui_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Silk_from_Mawangdui_2.jpg/330px-Silk_from_Mawangdui_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Silk_from_Mawangdui_2.jpg/440px-Silk_from_Mawangdui_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Silk_from_Mawangdui_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han-dynasty</a> Chinese <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">silk</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mawangdui" title="Mawangdui">Mawangdui</a>, 2nd century BC, silk from <a href="/wiki/History_of_China" title="History of China">China</a> was perhaps the most lucrative luxury item the Parthians traded at the western end of the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-garthwaite_2005_78_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-garthwaite_2005_78-54">[54]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Following the Seleucid withdrawal from Mesopotamia, the Parthian governor of Babylonia, Himerus, was ordered by the Arsacid court to conquer Characene, then ruled by <a href="/wiki/Hyspaosines" title="Hyspaosines">Hyspaosines</a> from <a href="/wiki/Charax_Spasinu" title="Charax Spasinu">Charax Spasinu</a>. When this failed, Hyspaosines invaded Babylonia in 127&#160;BC and occupied Seleucia. Yet by 122&#160;BC, Mithridates II forced Hyspaosines out of Babylonia and made the kings of Characene <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassals</a> under Parthian <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> After Mithridates extended Parthian control further west, occupying <a href="/wiki/Dura-Europos" title="Dura-Europos">Dura-Europos</a> in 113&#160;BC, he became embroiled in a conflict with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Armenia_(antiquity)" title="Kingdom of Armenia (antiquity)">Kingdom of Armenia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> His forces defeated and deposed <a href="/wiki/Artavasdes_I_of_Armenia" title="Artavasdes I of Armenia">Artavasdes I of Armenia</a> in 97&#160;BC, taking his son Tigranes hostage, who would later become <a href="/wiki/Tigranes_the_Great" title="Tigranes the Great">Tigranes II "the Great" of Armenia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;95&#8211;55&#160;BC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Indo-Parthian_Kingdom" title="Indo-Parthian Kingdom">Indo-Parthian Kingdom</a>, located in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> made an alliance with the Parthian Empire in the 1st century BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_2007_26_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_2007_26-58">[58]</a></sup> Bivar claims that these two states considered each other political equals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> After the Greek philosopher <a href="/wiki/Apollonius_of_Tyana" title="Apollonius of Tyana">Apollonius of Tyana</a> visited the court of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vardanes_I_of_Parthia" title="Vardanes I of Parthia">Vardanes I of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;40&#8211;47&#160;AD) in 42&#160;AD, Vardanes provided him with the protection of a caravan as he traveled to Indo-Parthia. When Apollonius reached Indo-Parthia\'s capital <a href="/wiki/Taxila" title="Taxila">Taxila</a>, his caravan leader read Vardanes\' official letter, perhaps written in Parthian, to an Indian official who treated Apollonius with great hospitality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_2007_26_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_2007_26-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Imperial_China" title="Foreign relations of Imperial China">diplomatic venture</a> of <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Qian" title="Zhang Qian">Zhang Qian</a> into Central Asia during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wu_of_Han" title="Emperor Wu of Han">Emperor Wu of Han</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;141&#8211;87&#160;BC), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_Dynasty" title="Han Dynasty">Han Empire</a> of China sent a delegation to Mithridates II\'s court in 121&#160;BC. The Han embassy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Han_Dynasty#Foreign_trade_and_tributary_exchange" title="Economy of the Han Dynasty">opened official trade relations</a> with Parthia via the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> yet did not achieve a desired military alliance against the confederation of the Xiongnu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The Parthian Empire was enriched by taxing the Eurasian caravan trade in <a href="/wiki/History_of_silk" title="History of silk">silk</a>, the most highly priced luxury good <a href="/wiki/Roman_commerce" title="Roman commerce">imported by the Romans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Pearls were also a highly valued import from China, while the Chinese purchased Parthian spices, perfumes, and fruits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Exotic animals were also given as gifts from the Arsacid to Han courts; in 87 AD <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacorus_II_of_Parthia" title="Pacorus II of Parthia">Pacorus II of Parthia</a> sent lions and Persian gazelles to <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Zhang_of_Han" title="Emperor Zhang of Han">Emperor Zhang of Han</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;75&#8211;88&#160;AD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Besides silk, Parthian goods purchased by Roman merchants included <a href="/wiki/History_of_metallurgy_in_the_Indian_subcontinent" title="History of metallurgy in the Indian subcontinent">iron from India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spices</a>, and fine leather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Caravans traveling through the Parthian Empire brought West Asian and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Roman_glass" title="Roman glass">Roman luxury glasswares</a> to China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The merchants of <a href="/wiki/Sogdia" title="Sogdia">Sogdia</a>, speaking an <a href="/wiki/Sogdian_language" title="Sogdian language">Eastern Iranian language</a>, served as the primary middlemen of this vital silk trade between Parthia and Han China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rome_and_Armenia">Rome and Armenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Parthian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rome and Armenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Persian_relations" title="Roman&#8211;Persian relations">Roman&#8211;Persian relations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Parthian_Wars" title="Roman&#8211;Parthian Wars">Roman&#8211;Parthian Wars</a></div>\n<p>The Yuezhi <a href="/wiki/Kushan_Empire" title="Kushan Empire">Kushan Empire</a> in northern India largely guaranteed the security of Parthia\'s eastern border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_92_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_92-67">[67]</a></sup> Thus, from the mid-1st century BC onwards, the Arsacid court focused on securing the western border, primarily against Rome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brosius_2006_92_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-brosius_2006_92-67">[67]</a></sup> A year following Mithridates II\'s subjugation of Armenia, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucius_Cornelius_Sulla" title="Lucius Cornelius Sulla">Lucius Cornelius Sulla</a>, the Roman <a href="/wiki/Proconsul" title="Proconsul">proconsul</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">Cilicia</a>, convened with the Parthian diplomat <a href="/wiki/Orobazus" title="Orobazus">Orobazus</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Euphrates" title="Euphrates">Euphrates</a> river. The two agreed that the river would serve as the border between Parthia and Rome, although several historians have argued that Sulla only had authority to communicate these terms back to Rome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite this agreement, in 93 or 92&#160;BC Parthia fought a war in Syria against the tribal leader <a href="/wiki/Laodice_of_the_Sameans" title="Laodice of the Sameans">Laodice</a> and her Seleucid ally <a href="/wiki/Antiochus_X_Eusebes" title="Antiochus X Eusebes">Antiochus X Eusebes</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;95&#8211;92?&#160;BC), killing the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kennedy_1996_77&#8211;78_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-kennedy_1996_77&#8211;78-69">[69]</a></sup> When one of the last Seleucid monarchs, <a href="/wiki/Demetrius_III_Eucaerus" title="Demetrius III Eucaerus">Demetrius III Eucaerus</a>, attempted to besiege Beroea (modern <a href="/wiki/Aleppo" title="Aleppo">Aleppo</a>), Parthia sent military aid to the inhabitants and Demetrius was defeated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kennedy_1996_77&#8211;78_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-kennedy_1996_77&#8211;78-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orodesi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="226" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Orodesi.jpg/220px-Orodesi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Orodesi.jpg/330px-Orodesi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Orodesi.jpg/440px-Orodesi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orodesi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Drachma of <a href="/wiki/Orodes_I_of_Parthia" title="Orodes I of Parthia">Orodes I of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;c.&#160;90&#8211;80&#160;BC)</div></div></div>\n<p>Following the rule of Mithridates II, Gotarzes I ruled Babylonia, while <a href="/wiki/Orodes_I_of_Parthia" title="Orodes I of Parthia">Orodes I</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;90&#8211;80&#160;BC) ruled Parthia separately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> This system of split monarchy weakened Parthia, allowing Tigranes II of Armenia to annex Parthian territory in western Mesopotamia. This land would not be restored to Parthia until the reign of <a href="/wiki/Sanatruces_of_Parthia" title="Sanatruces of Parthia">Sanatruces of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;78&#8211;71&#160;BC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Mithridatic_War" title="Third Mithridatic War">Third Mithridatic War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mithridates_VI_of_Pontus" title="Mithridates VI of Pontus">Mithridates VI of Pontus</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;119&#8211;63&#160;BC), an ally of Tigranes II of Armenia, requested aid from Parthia against Rome, but Sanatruces refused help.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_44-45_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_44-45-72">[72]</a></sup> When the Roman commander <a href="/wiki/Lucullus" title="Lucullus">Lucullus</a> marched against the Armenian capital <a href="/wiki/Tigranocerta" title="Tigranocerta">Tigranocerta</a> in 69&#160;BC, Mithridates VI and Tigranes II requested the aid of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phraates_III_of_Parthia" title="Phraates III of Parthia">Phraates III of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;71&#8211;58). Phraates did not send aid to either, and after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tigranocerta" title="Battle of Tigranocerta">fall of Tigranocerta</a> he reaffirmed with Lucullus the Euphrates as the boundary between Parthia and Rome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tigranes the Younger, son of Tigranes II of Armenia, failed to usurp the Armenian throne from his father. He fled to Phraates III and convinced him to march against Armenia\'s new capital at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artashat_(ancient_city)" title="Artashat (ancient city)">Artaxarta</a>. When this siege failed, Tigranes the Younger once again fled, this time to the Roman commander <a href="/wiki/Pompey" title="Pompey">Pompey</a>. He promised Pompey that he would act as a guide through Armenia, but, when Tigranes II submitted to Rome as a <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client king</a>, Tigranes the Younger was brought to Rome as a hostage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Phraates demanded Pompey return Tigranes the Younger to him, but Pompey refused. In retaliation, Phraates launched an invasion into <a href="/wiki/Corduene" title="Corduene">Corduene</a> (southeastern Turkey) where, according to two conflicting Roman accounts, the Roman consul <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Afranius_(consul)" title="Lucius Afranius (consul)">Lucius Afranius</a> forced the Parthians out by either military or diplomatic means.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marcus_Licinius_Crassus_Louvre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2632" data-file-width="1892" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Marcus_Licinius_Crassus_Louvre.jpg/170px-Marcus_Licinius_Crassus_Louvre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Marcus_Licinius_Crassus_Louvre.jpg/255px-Marcus_Licinius_Crassus_Louvre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Marcus_Licinius_Crassus_Louvre.jpg/340px-Marcus_Licinius_Crassus_Louvre.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marcus_Licinius_Crassus_Louvre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Roman marble head of the triumvir <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Licinius_Crassus" title="Marcus Licinius Crassus">Marcus Licinius Crassus</a>, who was <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carrhae" title="Battle of Carrhae">defeated at Carrhae</a> by <a href="/wiki/Surena" title="Surena">Surena</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Phraates III was assassinated by his sons <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orodes_II_of_Parthia" title="Orodes II of Parthia">Orodes II of Parthia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mithridates_III_of_Parthia" title="Mithridates III of Parthia">Mithridates III of Parthia</a>, after which Orodes turned on Mithridates, forcing him to flee from Media to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syria_(Roman_province)" title="Syria (Roman province)">Roman Syria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aulus_Gabinius" title="Aulus Gabinius">Aulus Gabinius</a>, the Roman proconsul of Syria, marched in support of Mithridates to the Euphrates, but had to turn back to aid <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_XII_Auletes" title="Ptolemy XII Auletes">Ptolemy XII Auletes</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;80&#8211;58; 55&#8211;51&#160;BC) against a rebellion in Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite losing his Roman support, Mithridates managed to conquer Babylonia, and minted coins at Seleucia until 54&#160;BC. In that year, Orodes\' general, known only as <a href="/wiki/Surena" title="Surena">Surena</a> after his noble family\'s clan name, recaptured Seleucia, and Mithridates was executed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Marcus_Licinius_Crassus" title="Marcus Licinius Crassus">Marcus Licinius Crassus</a>, one of the <a href="/wiki/First_Triumvirate" title="First Triumvirate">triumvirs</a> who was now proconsul of Syria, launched an invasion into Parthia in 53&#160;BC in belated support of Mithridates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> As his army <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carrhae" title="Battle of Carrhae">marched to Carrhae</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Harran" title="Harran">Harran</a>, southeastern Turkey), Orodes II invaded Armenia, cutting off support from Rome\'s ally <a href="/wiki/Artavasdes_II_of_Armenia" title="Artavasdes II of Armenia">Artavasdes II of Armenia</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;53&#8211;34&#160;BC). Orodes persuaded Artavasdes to a marriage alliance between the crown prince <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacorus_I_of_Parthia" title="Pacorus I of Parthia">Pacorus I of Parthia</a> (d.&#160;38&#160;BC) and Artavasdes\' sister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Surena, with an army entirely on horseback, rode to meet Crassus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Surena\'s 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Cataphract" title="Cataphract">cataphracts</a>, armed with lances, and 9,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horse_archer" title="Horse archer">horse archers</a> were outnumbered roughly four to one by Crassus\' army, comprising seven <a href="/wiki/Roman_legion" title="Roman legion">Roman legions</a> and auxiliaries including mounted <a href="/wiki/Gauls" title="Gauls">Gauls</a> and light infantry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_52_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_52-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Relying on a baggage train of about 1,000 camels, the Parthian horse archers were given constant supplies of arrows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_52_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_52-82">[82]</a></sup> The horse archers employed the "<a href="/wiki/Parthian_shot" title="Parthian shot">Parthian shot</a>" tactic, where they would fake a retreat, only to turn and fire upon their opponents. This tactic, combined with the use of heavy <a href="/wiki/Composite_bow" title="Composite bow">composite bows</a> on flat plain devastated Crassus\' infantry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p>With some 20,000 Romans dead, approximately 10,000 captured, and roughly another 10,000 escaping west, Crassus fled into the Armenian countryside.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> At the head of his army, Surena approached Crassus, offering a <a href="/wiki/Parley" title="Parley">parley</a>, which Crassus accepted. However, he was killed when one of his junior officers, suspecting a trap, attempted to stop him from riding into Surena\'s camp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Crassus\' defeat at Carrhae was one of the worst military defeats of Roman history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kennedy_1996_78_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-kennedy_1996_78-86">[86]</a></sup> Parthia\'s victory cemented its reputation as a formidable if not equal power with Rome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> With his camp followers, war captives, and precious Roman booty, Surena traveled some 700&#160;km (430&#160;mi) back to Seleucia where his victory was celebrated. However, fearing his ambitions even for the Arsacid throne, Orodes had Surena executed shortly thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kennedy_1996_78_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-kennedy_1996_78-86">[86]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Antony_with_Octavian_aureus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="194" data-file-width="386" decoding="async" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Antony_with_Octavian_aureus.jpg/220px-Antony_with_Octavian_aureus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Antony_with_Octavian_aureus.jpg/330px-Antony_with_Octavian_aureus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8b/Antony_with_Octavian_aureus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Antony_with_Octavian_aureus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roman <a href="/wiki/Aureus" title="Aureus">aurei</a> bearing the portraits of <a href="/wiki/Mark_Antony" title="Mark Antony">Mark Antony</a> (left) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Octavian" title="Octavian">Octavian</a> (right), issued in 41&#160;BC to celebrate the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Triumvirate" title="Second Triumvirate">Second Triumvirate</a> by Octavian, Antony and <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aemilius_Lepidus_(triumvir)" title="Marcus Aemilius Lepidus (triumvir)">Marcus Lepidus</a> in 43&#160;BC</div></div></div>\n<p>Emboldened by the victory over Crassus, the Parthians attempted to capture Roman-held territories in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crown_prince" title="Crown prince">Crown prince</a> Pacorus I and his commander Osaces raided Syria as far as Antioch in 51 BC, but were repulsed by <a href="/wiki/Gaius_Cassius_Longinus" title="Gaius Cassius Longinus">Gaius Cassius Longinus</a>, who ambushed and killed Osaces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The Arsacids sided with Pompey in <a href="/wiki/Caesar%27s_Civil_War" title="Caesar\'s Civil War">his civil war</a> against <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> and even sent troops to support the anti-Caesarian forces at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Philippi" title="Battle of Philippi">Battle of Philippi</a> in 42&#160;BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Quintus_Labienus" title="Quintus Labienus">Quintus Labienus</a>, a general loyal to Cassius and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcus_Junius_Brutus_the_Younger" title="Marcus Junius Brutus the Younger">Brutus</a>, sided with Parthia against the <a href="/wiki/Second_Triumvirate" title="Second Triumvirate">Second Triumvirate</a> in 40 BC; the following year he invaded Syria alongside Pacorus I.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_57_strugnell_2006_244_kennedy_1996_80_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_57_strugnell_2006_244_kennedy_1996_80-91">[91]</a></sup> The triumvir <a href="/wiki/Mark_Antony" title="Mark Antony">Mark Antony</a> was unable to lead the Roman defense against Parthia due to his departure to Italy, where he amassed his forces to confront his rival <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Octavian" title="Octavian">Octavian</a> and eventually conducted negotiations with him at Brundisium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After Syria was occupied by Pacorus\' army, Labienus split from the main Parthian force to invade <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> while Pacorus and his commander <a href="/wiki/Barzapharnes" title="Barzapharnes">Barzapharnes</a> invaded the Roman <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_57_strugnell_2006_244_kennedy_1996_80_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_57_strugnell_2006_244_kennedy_1996_80-91">[91]</a></sup> They subdued all settlements along the Mediterranean coast as far south as Ptolemais (modern <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre, Israel</a>), with the lone exception of <a href="/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon" title="Tyre, Lebanon">Tyre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_57_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_57-93">[93]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Judea" title="Judea">Judea</a>, the pro-Roman Jewish forces of high priest <a href="/wiki/Hyrcanus_II" title="Hyrcanus II">Hyrcanus II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phasael" title="Phasael">Phasael</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Herod_the_Great" title="Herod the Great">Herod</a> were defeated by the Parthians and their Jewish ally <a href="/wiki/Antigonus_II_Mattathias" title="Antigonus II Mattathias">Antigonus II Mattathias</a> (r.&#160;40&#8211;37&#160;BC); the latter was made king of Judea while Herod fled to his fort at <a href="/wiki/Masada" title="Masada">Masada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_57_strugnell_2006_244_kennedy_1996_80_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_57_strugnell_2006_244_kennedy_1996_80-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite these successes, the Parthians were soon driven out of the Levant by a Roman counteroffensive. <a href="/wiki/Publius_Ventidius_Bassus" title="Publius Ventidius Bassus">Publius Ventidius Bassus</a>, an officer under Mark Antony, defeated and then executed Labienus at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Cilician_Gates" title="Battle of the Cilician Gates">Battle of the Cilician Gates</a> (in modern <a href="/wiki/Mersin_Province" title="Mersin Province">Mersin Province</a>, Turkey) in 39 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_57-58_strugnell_2006_239,_245_brosius_2006_96_kennedy_1996_80_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_57-58_strugnell_2006_239,_245_brosius_2006_96_kennedy_1996_80-94">[94]</a></sup> Shortly afterward, a Parthian force in Syria led by general Pharnapates was defeated by Ventidius at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Amanus_Pass" title="Battle of Amanus Pass">Battle of Amanus Pass</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_57-58_strugnell_2006_239,_245_brosius_2006_96_kennedy_1996_80_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_57-58_strugnell_2006_239,_245_brosius_2006_96_kennedy_1996_80-94">[94]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result, Pacorus I temporarily withdrew from Syria. When he returned in the spring of 38&#160;BC, he faced Ventidius at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mount_Gindarus" title="Battle of Mount Gindarus">Battle of Mount Gindarus</a>, northeast of Antioch. Pacorus was killed during the battle, and his forces retreated across the Euphrates. His death spurred a succession crisis in which Orodes II chose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phraates_IV_of_Parthia" title="Phraates IV of Parthia">Phraates IV of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;38&#8211;2&#160;BC) as his new heir.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phraatesiv.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="241" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Phraatesiv.jpg/220px-Phraatesiv.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Phraatesiv.jpg/330px-Phraatesiv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Phraatesiv.jpg/440px-Phraatesiv.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phraatesiv.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Drachma of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phraates_IV_of_Parthia" title="Phraates IV of Parthia">Phraates IV of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>.&#160;c.&#160;38&#8211;2&#160;BC). Reverse side: Tyche/Khvarenah bestowing the attributes of power (palm, cornucopia) on the king; inscription &#914;&#913;&#931;&#921;&#923;&#917;&#937;&#931; &#914;&#913;&#931;&#921;&#923;&#917;&#937;&#925; &#913;&#929;&#931;&#913;&#922;&#927;&#933; &#917;&#933;&#917;&#929;&#915;&#917;&#932;&#927;&#933; &#917;&#928;&#921;&#934;&#913;&#925;&#927;&#933;&#931; &#934;&#921;&#923;&#917;&#923;&#923;&#919;&#925;&#927;&#931; "of the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Kings" title="King of Kings">King of Kings</a> Arsaces the Renowned/Manifest Benefactor Philhellene"</div></div></div>\n<p>Upon assuming the throne, Phraates IV eliminated rival claimants by killing and exiling his own brothers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> One of them, Monaeses, fled to Antony and convinced him to <a href="/wiki/Antony%27s_Parthian_War" title="Antony\'s Parthian War">invade Parthia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Antony defeated Parthia\'s Judaean ally Antigonus in 37&#160;BC, installing Herod as a client king in his place.\n</p><p>The following year, when Antony marched to <a href="/wiki/Erzurum" title="Erzurum">Erzurum</a>, Artavasdes II of Armenia once again switched alliances by sending Antony additional troops. Antony invaded Media <a href="/wiki/Atropatene" title="Atropatene">Atropatene</a> (modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_Azerbaijan" title="Iranian Azerbaijan">Iranian Azerbaijan</a>), then ruled by Parthia\'s ally <a href="/wiki/Artavasdes_I_of_Media_Atropatene" title="Artavasdes I of Media Atropatene">Artavasdes I of Media Atropatene</a>, with the intention of seizing the capital Praaspa, the location of which is now unknown. However, Phraates IV ambushed Antony\'s rear detachment, destroying a giant <a href="/wiki/Battering_ram" title="Battering ram">battering ram</a> meant for <a href="/wiki/Siege_engine" title="Siege engine">the siege</a> of Praaspa; after this, Artavasdes abandoned Antony\'s forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Parthians pursued and harassed Antony\'s army as it fled to Armenia. Eventually, the greatly weakened force reached Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> After this, Antony lured Artavasdes II into a trap with the promise of a marriage alliance. He was taken captive in 34 BC, paraded in Antony\'s mock <a href="/wiki/Roman_triumph" title="Roman triumph">Roman triumph</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, Egypt,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and eventually executed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleopatra_VII" title="Cleopatra VII">Cleopatra VII</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Kingdom" title="Ptolemaic Kingdom">Ptolemaic Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_64-65_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_64-65-102">[102]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Antony attempted to strike an alliance with Artavasdes I of Media Atropatene, whose relations with Phraates IV had recently soured. This was abandoned when Antony and his forces withdrew from Armenia in 33&#160;BC; they escaped a Parthian invasion while Antony\'s rival Octavian attacked his forces to the west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bivar_1983_64-65_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-bivar_1983_64-65-102">[102]</a></sup> Following Antony\'s suicide in Egypt followed by that of <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Cleopatra" title="Death of Cleopatra">his wife Cleopatra</a> in 30 BC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> the Parthian ally <a href="/wiki/Artaxias_II" title="Artaxias II">Artaxias II</a> reassumed the throne of Armenia.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Peace_with_Rome.2C_court_intrigue_and_contact_with_Chinese_generals"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Peace_with_Rome,_court_intrigue_and_contact_with_Chinese_generals">Peace with Rome, court intrigue and contact with Chinese generals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Parthian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Peace with Rome, court intrigue and contact with Chinese generals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Pax_Romana" title="Pax Romana">Pax Romana</a></div>\n<p>Following the defeat of Antony and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reign_of_Cleopatra_VII" title="Reign of Cleopatra VII">Cleopatra</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Egypt" title="Ptolemaic Egypt">Ptolemaic Egypt</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Actium" title="Battle of Actium">Battle of Actium</a> in 31&#160;BC, Octavian consolidated his political power and in 27&#160;BC was named <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">Roman Senate</a>, becoming the first <a href="/wiki/Roman_emperor" title="Roman emperor">Roman emperor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Around this time, <a href="/wiki/Tiridates_II_of_Parthia" title="Tiridates II of Parthia">Tiridates II of Parthia</a> briefly overthrew Phraates IV, who was able to quickly reestablish his rule with the aid of Scythian nomads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Tiridates fled to the Romans, taking one of Phraates\' sons with him. In negotiations conducted in 20&#160;BC, Phraates arranged for the release of his kidnapped son. In return, the Romans received the lost <a href="/wiki/Aquila_(Roman)" title="Aquila (Roman)">legionary standards</a> taken at Carrhae in 53&#160;BC, as well as any surviving prisoners of war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The Parthians viewed this exchange as a small price to pay to regain the prince.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Augustus hailed the return of the standards as a political victory over Parthia; this propaganda was celebrated in the minting of new coins, the <a href="/wiki/Forum_of_Augustus" title="Forum of Augustus">building of a new temple</a> to house the standards, and even in fine art such as the <a href="/wiki/Breastplate" title="Breastplate">breastplate</a> scene on his statue <a href="/wiki/Augustus_of_Prima_Porta" title="Augustus of Prima Porta">Augustus of Prima Porta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Augustus_Prima_Porta_(detail).PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="229" data-file-width="233" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Augustus_Prima_Porta_%28detail%29.PNG/220px-Augustus_Prima_Porta_%28detail%29.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/22/Augustus_Prima_Porta_%28detail%29.PNG 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Augustus_Prima_Porta_(detail).PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A close-up view of the <a href="/wiki/Breastplate" title="Breastplate">breastplate</a> on the statue of <a href="/wiki/Augustus_of_Prima_Porta" title="Augustus of Prima Porta">Augustus of Prima Porta</a>, showing a Parthian man returning to <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> the <a href="/wiki/Aquila_(Roman)" title="Aquila (Roman)">legionary standards</a> lost by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Licinius_Crassus" title="Marcus Licinius Crassus">Marcus Licinius Crassus</a> at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carrhae" title="Battle of Carrhae">Carrhae</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Along with the prince, Augustus also gave Phraates IV an Italian slave-girl, who later became Queen <a href="/wiki/Musa_of_Parthia" title="Musa of Parthia">Musa of Parthia</a>. To ensure that her child Phraataces would inherit the throne without incident, Musa convinced Phraates IV to give his other sons to Augustus as hostages. Again, Augustus used this as propaganda depicting the submission of Parthia to Rome, listing it as a great accomplishment in his <i><a href="/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti" title="Res Gestae Divi Augusti">Res Gestae Divi Augusti</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> When Phraataces took the throne as <a href="/wiki/Phraates_V" title="Phraates V">Phraates V</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;2&#160;BC &#8211; 4&#160;AD), Musa married her own son and ruled alongside him. The Parthian nobility, disapproving of both the incestuous relationship and the notion of a king with non-Arsacid blood, forced the pair into exile in Roman territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Phraates\' successor <a href="/wiki/Orodes_III_of_Parthia" title="Orodes III of Parthia">Orodes III of Parthia</a> lasted just two years on the throne, and was followed by <a href="/wiki/Vonones_I" title="Vonones I">Vonones I</a>, who had adopted many Roman mannerisms during time in Rome. The Parthian nobility, angered by Vonones\' sympathies for the Romans, backed a rival claimant, <a href="/wiki/Artabanus_III_of_Parthia" title="Artabanus III of Parthia">Artabanus III of Parthia</a> (<i>r</i>. c.&#160;10&#8211;38&#160;AD), who eventually defeated Vonones and drove him into exile in Roman Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the reign of Artabanus III, two Jewish commoners and brothers, <a href="/wiki/Anilai_and_Asinai" title="Anilai and Asinai">Anilai and Asinai</a> from <a href="/wiki/Nehardea" title="Nehardea">Nehardea</a> (near modern <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a>, Iraq),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> led a revolt against the Parthian governor of Babylonia. After defeating the latter, the two were granted the right to govern the region by Artabanus III, who feared further rebellion elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Anilai\'s Parthian wife poisoned Asinai out of fear he would attack Anilai over his marriage to a <a href="/wiki/Gentile" title="Gentile">gentile</a>. Following this, Anilai became embroiled in an armed conflict with a son-in-law of Artabanus, who eventually defeated him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> With the Jewish regime removed, the native Babylonians began to harass the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_Jews" title="Iraqi Jews">local Jewish community</a>, forcing them to emigrate to Seleucia. When that city rebelled against Parthian rule in 35&#8211;36&#160;AD, the Jews were expelled again, this time by the local <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramaeans" title="Aramaeans">Aramaeans</a>.
